\[f(4) = 2(16) - 3(4) + 1 = 32 - 12 + 1 = 21\]

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{f(x) = 2x\^{}2 - 3x + 1}, then type \texttt{f(4)}. Desmos displays $21$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds either way.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 4: Percentage}

A shirt originally costs \$40. It is on sale for 25\% off. What is the sale price?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item \$10
\item \$15
\item \$25
\item \$30
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: D}

\textbf{By Hand:} $40 \times 0.25 = 10$ discount. Sale price $= 40 - 10 = 30$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{40 - 40 * 0.25} or \texttt{40 * 0.75}. Desmos shows $30$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 5: System of Equations}

\[
\begin{cases} y = 2x + 1 \\ y = -x + 7 \end{cases}
\]

What is the $x$-coordinate of the solution?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $1$
\item $2$
\item $3$
\item $4$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} Set equal: $2x + 1 = -x + 7 \implies 3x = 6 \implies x = 2$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = 2x + 1} on line 1 and \texttt{y = -x + 7} on line 2. Click the intersection point. Desmos shows $(2, 5)$. The $x$-coordinate is $2$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds with Desmos (type both lines, click intersection).
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 6: Absolute Value}

What is the value of $|{-7}| + |3 - 10|$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $4$
\item $10$
\item $14$
\item $17$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{By Hand:} $|-7| + |3 - 10| = 7 + |-7| = 7 + 7 = 14$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{abs(-7) + abs(3 - 10)}. Desmos shows $14$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 7: Linear Inequality}

Which of the following is a solution to $2x - 5 > 9$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x = 5$
\item $x = 7$
\item $x = 8$
\item Both B and C
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: D}

\textbf{By Hand:} $2x - 5 > 9 \implies 2x > 14 \implies x > 7$. So $x = 7$ does NOT satisfy (it's not strictly greater), but $x = 8$ does. Wait---let's recheck: $x > 7$ means $x = 7$ gives $2(7) - 5 = 9$, which is NOT greater than 9. So only $x = 8$ works.

\textbf{Corrected Answer: C}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{2x - 5 > 9}. Desmos shades the number line for $x > 7$. Then check: $x = 7$ is the boundary (not included), $x = 8$ is in the shaded region.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 8: Mean of a Data Set}

What is the mean of the data set $\{4, 8, 12, 16, 20\}$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $10$
\item $12$
\item $14$
\item $16$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} $\frac{4 + 8 + 12 + 16 + 20}{5} = \frac{60}{5} = 12$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{mean([4, 8, 12, 16, 20])}. Desmos shows $12$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds by hand, 12 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 9: Exponent Rules}

Simplify: $\dfrac{x^5 \cdot x^3}{x^2}$

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x^4$
\item $x^6$
\item $x^8$
\item $x^{10}$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} $\frac{x^5 \cdot x^3}{x^2} = \frac{x^8}{x^2} = x^6$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} This is an algebraic simplification problem. Desmos doesn't simplify symbolic expressions. However, you can \textbf{verify} by testing a value. Type \texttt{f(x) = (x\^{}5 * x\^{}3) / x\^{}2} and \texttt{g(x) = x\^{}6}. Then type \texttt{f(3)} and \texttt{g(3)}. If both give $729$, the answer is confirmed
.

\textbf{Time Target:} 20 seconds with Desmos verification.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 10: Quadratic --- Finding the Vertex}

What is the vertex of the parabola $y = 2(x - 4)^2 + 5$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $(4, 5)$
\item $(-4, 5)$
\item $(4, -5)$
\item $(-4, -5)$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{By Hand:} The vertex form is $y = a(x - h)^2 + k$, where the vertex is $(h, k)$. Here $h = 4$ and $k = 5$, so the vertex is $(4, 5)$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = 2(x - 4)\^{}2 + 5}. Click the minimum point of the parabola. Desmos displays $(4, 5)$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 5 seconds by hand (if you know vertex form), 8 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 11: Systems of Equations}

What is the solution to the system?
\[
\begin{cases}
3x + 2y = 12 \\
x - y = 1
\end{cases}
\]

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $(2, 3)$
\item $(2, 1)$
\item $\left(\dfrac{14}{5}, \dfrac{9}{5}\right)$
\item $(3, 2)$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{3x + 2y = 12} on line 1 and \texttt{x - y = 1} on line 2. Click the intersection point. Desmos shows $(2.8, 1.8)$, which is $\left(\frac{14}{5}, \frac{9}{5}\right)$.

\textbf{By Hand (Substitution):} From the second equation: $x = y + 1$. Substitute into the first: $3(y + 1) + 2y = 12 \implies 3y + 3 + 2y = 12 \implies 5y = 9 \implies y = \frac{9}{5}$. Then $x = \frac{9}{5} + 1 = \frac{14}{5}$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 12 seconds with Desmos, 45 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 12: Exponential Growth}

A population of bacteria doubles every 3 hours. If the initial population is 500, which function models the population $P$ after $t$ hours?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $P(t) = 500(2)^t$
\item $P(t) = 500(2)^{t/3}$
\item $P(t) = 500(3)^{t/2}$
\item $P(t) = 1000(2)^t$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} The general form is $P(t) = P_0 \cdot b^{t/d}$ where $P_0 = 500$ is the initial population, $b = 2$ (doubles), and $d = 3$ (every 3 hours). So $P(t) = 500(2)^{t/3}$.

\textbf{Desmos Verification:} Type \texttt{P(t) = 500 * 2\^{}(t/3)}. Check: $P(0) = 500$ \checkmark, $P(3) = 1000$ \checkmark, $P(6) = 2000$ \checkmark. The population doubles every 3 hours as required.

\textbf{Time Target:} 20 seconds.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 13: Circle Equation}

What is the center and radius of the circle $(x + 3)^2 + (y - 7)^2 = 49$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item Center $(3, -7)$, radius $49$
\item Center $(-3, 7)$, radius $7$
\item Center $(-3, 7)$, radius $49$
\item Center $(3, 7)$, radius $7$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} The standard form is $(x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2$. Here $h = -3$, $k = 7$, and $r^2 = 49 \implies r = 7$. Center $(-3, 7)$, radius $7$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{(x + 3)\^{}2 + (y - 7)\^{}2 = 49}. Desmos graphs the circle. Click any point on the circle and the center to visually confirm $(-3, 7)$ and measure that the radius is $7$.

\textbf{Common Mistake:} Confusing the signs---$(x + 3)$ means $h = -3$, not $h = 3$. Also, the radius is $\sqrt{49} = 7$, not $49$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds by hand, 15 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 14: Trigonometry}

In a right triangle, if $\sin(\theta) = \dfrac{5}{13}$, what is $\cos(\theta)$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $\dfrac{5}{12}$
\item $\dfrac{12}{13}$
\item $\dfrac{13}{12}$
\item $\dfrac{8}{13}$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} If $\sin(\theta) = \frac{5}{13}$, then opposite $= 5$ and hypotenuse $= 13$. By the Pythagorean theorem: adjacent $= \sqrt{13^2 - 5^2} = \sqrt{169 - 25} = \sqrt{144} = 12$. So $\cos(\theta) = \frac{12}{13}$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{arcsin(5/13)} to find $\theta \approx 22.62°$. Then type \texttt{cos(22.62°)}. Desmos shows $\approx 0.923$, and $\frac{12}{13} \approx 0.923$ \checkmark.

\textbf{Important:} Make sure Desmos is in degree mode if you're working with degrees. Click the wrench icon and select ``Degrees.''

\textbf{Time Target:} 20 seconds by hand, 15 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 15: Polynomial}

If $f(x) = x^3 - 4x^2 + x + 6$, what are the zeros of $f$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x = -1, 2, 3$
\item $x = 1, -2, 3$
\item $x = 1, 2, -3$
\item $x = -1, -2, 3$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy (Fastest):} Type \texttt{y = x\^{}3 - 4x\^{}2 + x + 6}. Click each $x$-intercept. Desmos shows $(-1, 0)$, $(2, 0)$, and $(3, 0)$. The zeros are $x = -1, 2, 3$.

\textbf{By Hand:} Test $x = -1$: $(-1)^3 - 4(-1)^2 + (-1) + 6 = -1 - 4 - 1 + 6 = 0$ \checkmark. Factor out $(x + 1)$: $x^3 - 4x^2 + x + 6 = (x + 1)(x^2 - 5x + 6) = (x + 1)(x - 2)(x - 3)$. Zeros: $x = -1, 2, 3$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds with Desmos, 90+ seconds by hand. This is a \textbf{massive} time save.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 16: Regression / Line of Best Fit}

The table below shows the relationship between hours studied and test scores:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{c|ccccc}
Hours ($x$) & 1 & 2 & 3 & 4 & 5 \\
\hline
Score ($y$) & 55 & 62 & 68 & 75 & 83
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Using the line of best fit, what score would you predict for a student who studies 7 hours?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $90$
\item $95$
\item $97$
\item $100$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Click the ``+'' button and add a \textbf{table}
\item Enter $x$-values: $1, 2, 3, 4, 5$ and $y$-values: $55, 62, 68, 75, 83$
\item In a new expression line, type \texttt{y\textasciitilde mx + b}
\item Desmos shows $m \approx 6.8$ and $b \approx 48.0$
\item In a new line, type \texttt{6.8(7) + 48.0}
\item Desmos shows $\approx 95.6$, closest to $95$
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Time Target:} 35 seconds (most time entering the table).
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 17: Function Composition}

If $f(x) = 2x + 1$ and $g(x) = x^2 - 3$, what is $f(g(2))$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $3$
\item $5$
\item $7$
\item $9$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{By Hand:} First find $g(2) = (2)^2 - 3 = 4 - 3 = 1$. Then $f(g(2)) = f(1) = 2(1) + 1 = 3$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{f(x) = 2x + 1} on line 1 and \texttt{g(x) = x\^{}2 - 3} on line 2. Then type \texttt{f(g(2))} on line 3. Desmos shows $3$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds by hand, 12 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 18: Rational Equation}

What value of $x$ satisfies $\dfrac{3}{x-2} = \dfrac{6}{x+1}$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x = 3$
\item $x = 5$
\item $x = 7$
\item $x = 8$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{3/(x-2) = 6/(x+1)}. Desmos doesn't directly solve equations typed this way. Instead, graph both sides: type \texttt{y = 3/(x-2)} and \texttt{y = 6/(x+1)}. Click the intersection. Desmos shows $(5, 2)$, so $x = 5$.

\textbf{By Hand:} Cross-multiply: $3(x + 1) = 6(x - 2) \implies 3x + 3 = 6x - 12 \implies 15 = 3x \implies x = 5$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds with Desmos, 25 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 19: Absolute Value Equation}

How many solutions does $|2x - 6| = 10$ have, and what are they?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item One solution: $x = 8$
\item One solution: $x = -2$
\item Two solutions: $x = 8$ and $x = -2$
\item No solution
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = abs(2x - 6)} and \texttt{y = 10}. Click both intersections. Desmos shows $(-2, 10)$ and $(8, 10)$. Two solutions: $x = -2$ and $x = 8$.

\textbf{By Hand:} $|2x - 6| = 10$ means $2x - 6 = 10$ or $2x - 6 = -10$.
\begin{itemize}
\item $2x - 6 = 10 \implies 2x = 16 \implies x = 8$
\item $2x - 6 = -10 \implies 2x = -4 \implies x = -2$
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Time Target:} 12 seconds with Desmos, 20 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 20: Completing the Square / Converting Forms}

Which of the following is equivalent to $x^2 + 8x + 7$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $(x + 4)^2 - 9$
\item $(x + 4)^2 + 9$
\item $(x + 8)^2 - 9$
\item $(x + 4)^2 - 7$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy (Fastest):} Type \texttt{y = x\^{}2 + 8x + 7} on line 1. Then type each answer choice on separate lines:
\begin{itemize}
\item Line 2: \texttt{y = (x + 4)\^{}2 - 9}
\item Line 3: \texttt{y = (x + 4)\^{}2 + 9}
\item Line 4: \texttt{y = (x + 8)\^{}2 - 9}
\item Line 5: \texttt{y = (x + 4)\^{}2 - 7}
\end{itemize}
The graph that \textbf{perfectly overlaps} with line 1 is the answer. Line 2 overlaps exactly $\to$ Answer A.

\textbf{By Hand:} Complete the square: $x^2 + 8x + 7 = (x^2 + 8x + 16) - 16 + 7 = (x + 4)^2 - 9$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 20 seconds with Desmos, 30 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\subsection{Section 2: Medium-Difficulty SAT Problems}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 21: System with No Solution}

For what value of $k$ does the system below have no solution?
\[
\begin{cases}
4x + 6y = 12 \\
2x + 3y = k
\end{cases}
\]

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $k = 6$
\item $k = 12$
\item $k = 3$
\item Any value of $k$ except $6$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: D}

\textbf{Analysis:} The first equation simplifies to $2x + 3y = 6$ (divide by 2). The second equation is $2x + 3y = k$. These are parallel lines (same slope) that never intersect \textbf{unless} $k = 6$ (which would make them the same line, giving infinitely many solutions). So for \textbf{no solution}, $k$ can be any value \textbf{except} $6$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{4x + 6y = 12} and \texttt{2x + 3y = k}. Add a slider for $k$. Slide $k$: when $k = 6$, the lines overlap. For any other value, the lines are parallel with no intersection.

\textbf{Time Target:} 25 seconds with Desmos slider exploration.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 22: Quadratic with Complex Discriminant}

How many real solutions does $3x^2 - 2x + 5 = 0$ have?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $0$
\item $1$
\item $2$
\item Infinitely many
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy (Fastest):} Type \texttt{y = 3x\^{}2 - 2x + 5}. The parabola opens upward and sits entirely \textbf{above} the $x$-axis---it never crosses. Therefore, there are \textbf{0 real solutions}.

\textbf{By Hand:} Discriminant $= b^2 - 4ac = (-2)^2 - 4(3)(5) = 4 - 60 = -56 < 0$. Negative discriminant means no real solutions.

\textbf{Time Target:} 8 seconds with Desmos (just look at the graph), 15 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 23: Exponential Equation}

Solve: $2^{x+1} = 32$

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x = 3$
\item $x = 4$
\item $x = 5$
\item $x = 16$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = 2\^{}(x+1)} and \texttt{y = 32}. Click the intersection. Desmos shows $(4, 32)$, so $x = 4$.

\textbf{By Hand:} $32 = 2^5$, so $2^{x+1} = 2^5 \implies x + 1 = 5 \implies x = 4
$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds with Desmos, 12 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 24: Circle Equation}

A circle in the $xy$-plane has the equation $(x + 3)^2 + (y - 2)^2 = 49$. What is the radius of the circle?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $7$
\item $49$
\item $\sqrt{49}$
\item $24.5$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{By Hand:} The standard form of a circle is $(x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2$. Here $r^2 = 49$, so $r = 7$. (Note: choice C is also $7$, but choice A states it directly.)

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{(x + 3)\^{}2 + (y - 2)\^{}2 = 49}. Desmos draws the circle. You can visually confirm the center is at $(-3, 2)$ and count that the circle extends 7 units in every direction from the center. Alternatively, click on any point on the circle and measure its distance from the center.

\textbf{Key Insight:} $r^2 = 49$ does NOT mean $r = 49$. Always take the square root. This is a very common SAT trap.

\textbf{Time Target:} 8 seconds by hand, 12 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 25: Completing the Square for a Circle}

The equation $x^2 + y^2 + 6x - 10y + 18 = 0$ represents a circle. What are the center and radius?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item Center $(-3, 5)$, radius $4$
\item Center $(3, -5)$, radius $4$
\item Center $(-3, 5)$, radius $16$
\item Center $(3, 5)$, radius $4$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy (Fastest --- Skip All Algebra!):} Type \texttt{x\^{}2 + y\^{}2 + 6x - 10y + 18 = 0} directly into Desmos. Desmos graphs the circle automatically. Click on the circle to identify key points. The topmost point is approximately $(-3, 9)$, the bottommost is $(-3, 1)$, the leftmost is $(-7, 5)$, and the rightmost is $(1, 5)$. From these:
\begin{itemize}
\item Center $= (-3, 5)$ (midpoint of any diameter)
\item Radius $= 9 - 5 = 4$ (distance from center to top)
\end{itemize}

\textbf{By Hand (Completing the Square):}
\begin{align*}
(x^2 + 6x) + (y^2 - 10y) &= -18 \\
(x^2 + 6x + 9) + (y^2 - 10y + 25) &= -18 + 9 + 25 \\
(x + 3)^2 + (y - 5)^2 &= 16
\end{align*}
Center $= (-3, 5)$, radius $= \sqrt{16} = 4$.

\textbf{Time Comparison:} By hand: 60--90 seconds. With Desmos: 20 seconds. \textbf{Desmos saves over a minute on this problem type!}
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 26: Function Composition}

If $f(x) = 3x + 2$ and $g(x) = x^2 - 1$, what is $f(g(4))$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $47$
\item $45$
\item $38$
\item $14$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{f(x) = 3x + 2} on line 1. Type \texttt{g(x) = x\^{}2 - 1} on line 2. Type \texttt{f(g(4))} on line 3. Desmos outputs $47$.

\textbf{By Hand:} First find $g(4) = 4^2 - 1 = 15$. Then $f(15) = 3(15) + 2 = 47$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds with Desmos, 20 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 27: Percentage Increase}

A store raises the price of a \$40 item by 15\%, then puts the new price on sale for 10\% off. What is the final price?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item \$40.00
\item \$41.40
\item \$42.00
\item \$46.00
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{40 * 1.15 * 0.90}. Desmos shows $41.4$.

\textbf{By Hand:}
\begin{itemize}
\item After 15\% increase: $40 \times 1.15 = 46$
\item After 10\% discount: $46 \times 0.90 = 41.40$
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Common Trap:} Students think 15\% up then 10\% down returns to the original price. It does NOT! A 15\% increase followed by a 10\% decrease gives a net increase of $1.15 \times 0.90 = 1.035$, or 3.5\%.

\textbf{Time Target:} 8 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 28: Trigonometry --- Right Triangle}

In a right triangle, one leg is 5 and the hypotenuse is 13. What is $\sin(\theta)$ where $\theta$ is the angle opposite the leg of length 5?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $\dfrac{5}{13}$
\item $\dfrac{12}{13}$
\item $\dfrac{5}{12}$
\item $\dfrac{13}{5}$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{By Hand:} $\sin(\theta) = \frac{\text{opposite}}{\text{hypotenuse}} = \frac{5}{13}$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} First find the other leg: type \texttt{sqrt(13\^{}2 - 5\^{}2)} to get $12$. Then $\sin(\theta) = \frac{5}{13}$. You can verify by typing \texttt{arcsin(5/13)} to get the angle, then \texttt{sin(} that angle \texttt{)} to confirm it returns $\frac{5}{13} \approx 0.3846$.

\textbf{Important:} Make sure Desmos is in \textbf{degree mode} if the problem gives angles in degrees. Click the wrench icon to toggle between degrees and radians.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds by hand using SOH-CAH-TOA.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 29: Rational Equation}

Solve: $\dfrac{3}{x-2} = \dfrac{9}{x+4}$

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x = 5$
\item $x = 6$
\item $x = 7$
\item $x = 8$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy (Fastest):} Type \texttt{y = 3/(x - 2)} and \texttt{y = 9/(x + 4)}. Click the intersection point. Desmos shows $(5, 1)$, so $x = 5$.

\textbf{By Hand:} Cross-multiply: $3(x + 4) = 9(x - 2)$. Then $3x + 12 = 9x - 18$, so $30 = 6x$, giving $x = 5$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 12 seconds with Desmos, 25 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 30: Standard Deviation Concept}

Data Set A: $\{50, 50, 50, 50, 50\}$ \\
Data Set B: $\{10, 30, 50, 70, 90\}$

Both data sets have the same mean. Which statement is true about their standard deviations?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item Data Set A has a greater standard deviation
\item Data Set B has a greater standard deviation
\item They have the same standard deviation
\item Cannot be determined
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{stdev([50, 50, 50, 50, 50])} --- Desmos shows $0$. Type \texttt{stdev([10, 30, 50, 70, 90])} --- Desmos shows approximately $31.62$. Data Set B has a much greater standard deviation.

\textbf{Conceptual Understanding:} Standard deviation measures \textbf{spread}. Data Set A has zero spread (all values are identical). Data Set B has values spread far from the mean. Greater spread = greater standard deviation.

\textbf{SAT Insight:} The SAT often tests your \textbf{conceptual} understanding of standard deviation without requiring you to calculate it. But Desmos CAN calculate it if needed.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds conceptually, 20 seconds with Desmos verification.
\end{solution}

\subsection{Hard Difficulty SAT Problems (Continued)}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 31: Polynomial with Given Root}

If $x = -3$ is a root of $f(x) = x^3 + 2x^2 - 9x - 18$, which of the following is a complete factorization?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $(x + 3)(x^2 - x - 6)$
\item $(x + 3)(x - 3)(x + 2)$
\item $(x + 3)(x + 3)(x - 2)$
\item $(x + 3)(x - 3)(x - 2)$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = x\^{}3 + 2x\^{}2 - 9x - 18}. Click all three $x$-intercepts. Desmos shows roots at $x = -3$, $x = 3$, and $x = -2$. Therefore the factored form is $(x + 3)(x - 3)(x + 2)$.

\textbf{Verification:} Expand choice B: $(x + 3)(x - 3) = x^2 - 9$. Then $(x^2 - 9)(x + 2) = x^3 + 2x^2 - 9x - 18$. \checkmark

\textbf{Why Desmos is Perfect Here:} Polynomial factoring by hand requires synthetic division or trial-and-error. Desmos shows all roots in seconds.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds with Desmos (graph and click three roots).
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 32: System of Nonlinear Equations}

How many solutions does the following system have?
\[
\begin{cases}
y = x^2 - 4 \\
y = 2x - 1
\end{cases}
\]

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $0$
\item $1$
\item $2$
\item $3$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = x\^{}2 - 4} and \texttt{y = 2x - 1}. Count the intersection points. Desmos shows two intersections at $(3, 5)$ and $(-1, -3)$.

\textbf{By Hand:} Set equal: $x^2 - 4 = 2x - 1 \implies x^2 - 2x - 3 = 0 \implies (x-3)(x+1) = 0$. Two solutions: $x = 3$ and $x = -1$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 8 seconds with Desmos (just count intersections), 30 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 33: Absolute Value Equation}

How many values of $x$ satisfy $|2x - 6| = x + 1$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $0$
\item $1$
\item $2$
\item $3$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = abs(2x - 6)} and \texttt{y = x + 1}. Count the intersection points. Desmos shows two intersections.

\textbf{By Hand:}

Case 1: $2x - 6 = x + 1 \implies x = 7$. Check: $|14 - 6| = 8$ and $7 + 1 = 8$. \checkmark

Case 2: $-(2x - 6) = x + 1 \implies -2x + 6 = x + 1 \implies 5 = 3x \implies x = \frac{5}{3}$. Check: $|2(\frac{5}{3}) - 6| = |\frac{10}{3} - 6| = |\frac{-8}{3}| = \frac{8}{3}$ and $\frac{5}{3} + 1 = \frac{8}{3}$. \checkmark

Two solutions.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds with Desmos, 60 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 34: Regression and Prediction}

The following data shows hours studied and test scores:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{c|ccccc}
Hours ($x$) & 1 & 2 & 3 & 5 & 7 \\
\hline
Score ($y$) & 55 & 62 & 68 & 80 & 91
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Using a linear model, what score would you predict for a student who studied 6 hours?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $82$
\item $85$
\item $87$
\item $90$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Click the ``+'' button and select ``table.''
\item Enter the data: $x$-values in column 1, $y$-values in column 2.
\item In a new line, type \texttt{y\textasciitilde mx + b}. Desmos computes $m \approx 5.89$ and $b \approx 49.96$.
\item Type \texttt{5.89 * 6 + 49.96} to get approximately $85.3$.
\end{enumerate}

The predicted score is closest to $85$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 45 seconds (most time spent entering the table).

\textbf{SAT Tip:} When you see a scatterplot or data table on the SAT with a question about ``line of best fit'' or ``predicted value,'' Desmos regression is your best friend.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 35: Complex Rational Expression}

If $\dfrac{x^2 - 9}{x^2 - x - 6} = \dfrac{A}{x + 2}$ for all $x$ where both sides are defined, what is the value of $A$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x + 3$
\item $x - 3$
\item $x + 2$
\item $1$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{
By Hand:} Factor numerator: $x^2 - 9 = (x+3)(x-3)$. Factor denominator: $x^2 - x - 6 = (x-3)(x+2)$.

So $\dfrac{(x+3)(x-3)}{(x-3)(x+2)} = \dfrac{x+3}{x+2}$.

Comparing with $\dfrac{A}{x+2}$, we get $A = x + 3$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{f(x) = (x\^{}2 - 9)/(x\^{}2 - x - 6)} and \texttt{g(x) = (x + 3)/(x + 2)}. If the graphs overlap perfectly (they will, except at $x = 3$ where there's a hole), then $A = x + 3$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 30 seconds by hand, 15 seconds with Desmos verification.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 36: Trigonometry --- Sine and Cosine}

In a right triangle, if $\sin(\theta) = \dfrac{5}{13}$, what is $\cos(\theta)$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $\dfrac{5}{12}$
\item $\dfrac{12}{13}$
\item $\dfrac{8}{13}$
\item $\dfrac{13}{12}$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} If $\sin(\theta) = \frac{5}{13}$, then opposite $= 5$ and hypotenuse $= 13$. By the Pythagorean theorem: adjacent $= \sqrt{13^2 - 5^2} = \sqrt{169 - 25} = \sqrt{144} = 12$. So $\cos(\theta) = \frac{12}{13}$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{arcsin(5/13)} to find $\theta \approx 22.62°$. Then type \texttt{cos(22.62°)} which gives approximately $0.923 = \frac{12}{13}$.

\textbf{Important Desmos Note:} Make sure your Desmos is in \textbf{degree mode} for SAT trig problems. Click the wrench icon and select ``Degrees.''

\textbf{Time Target:} 20 seconds by hand, 15 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 37: Function Composition}

If $f(x) = 2x + 3$ and $g(x) = x^2 - 1$, what is $f(g(2))$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $7$
\item $9$
\item $11$
\item $13$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} First find $g(2) = 2^2 - 1 = 4 - 1 = 3$. Then $f(3) = 2(3) + 3 = 9$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{f(x) = 2x + 3} and \texttt{g(x) = x\^{}2 - 1}. Then type \texttt{f(g(2))}. Desmos shows $9$.

\textbf{Key Insight:} Desmos handles function composition natively! You can define functions and then compose them directly. This is one of the most powerful features for SAT problems involving nested functions.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds by hand, 10 seconds with Desmos (after defining functions).
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 38: Percentage Increase}

A store increases the price of a \$60 item by 15\%, then offers a 10\% discount on the new price. What is the final price?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $\$60.00$
\item $\$62.10$
\item $\$63.00$
\item $\$69.00$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} After 15\% increase: $60 \times 1.15 = 69$. After 10\% discount: $69 \times 0.90 = 62.10$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{60 * 1.15 * 0.90}. Desmos shows $62.1$.

\textbf{SAT Trap Alert:} Many students think a 15\% increase followed by a 10\% decrease returns to the original price. It does NOT! The percentage decrease applies to the \textbf{larger} number, so you end up slightly above the original.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 39: Solving Radical Equations}

Solve: $\sqrt{3x + 7} = 5$

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x = 4$
\item $x = 6$
\item $x = 8$
\item $x = 10$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} Square both sides: $3x + 7 = 25 \implies 3x = 18 \implies x = 6$. Check: $\sqrt{3(6) + 7} = \sqrt{25} = 5$ \checkmark

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = sqrt(3x + 7)} and \texttt{y = 5}. Click the intersection point. Desmos shows $(6, 5)$, so $x = 6$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds either way.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 40: System of Equations --- Elimination}

Solve the system:
\[
\begin{cases}
3x + 2y = 16 \\
x - y = 2
\end{cases}
\]

What is the value of $x + y$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $4$
\item $6$
\item $8$
\item $10$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy (Fastest):} Type \texttt{3x + 2y = 16} and \texttt{x - y = 2}. Click the intersection point. Desmos shows $(4, 2)$. So $x + y = 4 + 2 = 6$.

\textbf{Wait---let's verify:} $3(4) + 2(2) = 12 + 4 = 16$ \checkmark. $4 - 2 = 2$ \checkmark. $x + y = 6$.

\textbf{Corrected Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand (Elimination):} From the second equation: $x = y + 2$. Substitute into the first: $3(y + 2) + 2y = 16 \implies 3y + 6 + 2y = 16 \implies 5y = 10 \implies y = 2$. Then $x = 4$. So $x + y = 6$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 12 seconds with Desmos, 30 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\subsection{SAT-Level Hard Problems (Problems 41--50)}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 41: Polynomial Division}

If $p(x) = x^3 - 4x^2 + x + 6$ and $p(2) = 0$, which of the following is a factor of $p(x)$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $(x - 1)$
\item $(x - 2)$
\item $(x + 2)$
\item $(x - 6)$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{Key Principle:} The Factor Theorem states that if $p(a) = 0$, then $(x - a)$ is a factor. Since $p(2) = 0$, $(x - 2)$ is a factor.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = x\^{}3 - 4x\^{}2 + x + 6}. Click the $x$-intercepts. If Desmos shows an intercept at $x = 2$, then $(x - 2)$ is a factor.

\textbf{Bonus:} Desmos will also show you the other roots, so you can fully factor the polynomial if needed.

\textbf{Time Target:} 5 seconds if you know the Factor Theorem, 10 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 42: Rational Equation}

Solve: $\dfrac{2}{x-1} + \dfrac{3}{x+1} = \dfrac{5x}{x^2-1}$

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x = 5$
\item $x = -5$
\item $x = 1$
\item No solution
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = 2/(x-1) + 3/(x+1)} and \texttt{y = 5x/(x\^{}2 - 1)}. Look for intersections. Desmos shows the graphs overlap everywhere they're both defined---this means the equation is an identity... Let's check more carefully.

\textbf{By Hand:} Note that $x^2 - 1 = (x-1)(x+1)$. Multiply both sides by $(x-1)(x+1)$:

$2(x+1) + 3(x-1) = 5x$

$2x + 2 + 3x - 3 = 5x$

$5x - 1 = 5x$

$-1 = 0$

This is a contradiction! There is \textbf{no solution}.

\textbf{Corrected Answer: D}

\textbf{Desmos Verification:} When you graph both sides, they appear to overlap, but that's because they are the \textbf{same expression} (both simplify to $\frac{5x-1}{x^2-1}$ vs $\frac{5x}{x^2-1}$). Look carefully---the graphs are close but NOT identical. Zoom in to see the gap.

\textbf{Lesson:} For rational equations, always verify algebraically or test specific values in Desmos. Type \texttt{2/(4) + 3/(5)} and compare to \texttt{5(5)/(24)}: $0.5 + 0.6 = 1.1$ vs $\frac{25}{24} \approx 1.042$. They don't match, confirming no solution.

\textbf{Time Target:} 45 seconds (this is a hard problem---use both Desmos and algebra).
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 43: Quadratic Systems}

How many solutions does the following system have?
\[
\begin{cases}
y = x^2 - 4x + 5 \\
y = 2x - 3
\end{cases}
\]

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $0$
\item $1$
\item $2$
\item Infinitely many
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy (10 seconds):} Type \texttt{y = x\^{}2 - 4x + 5} and \texttt{y = 2x - 3}. Count the intersection points. Desmos shows \textbf{two} intersections.

\textbf{By Hand:} Set equal: $x^2 - 4x + 5 = 2x - 3 \implies x^2 - 6x + 8 = 0 \implies (x-2)(x-4) = 0$. Two solutions: $x = 2$ and $x = 4$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 44: Exponential Growth Application}

A population of bacteria doubles every 3 hours. If the initial population is 500, what is the population after 12 hours?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $2{,}000$
\item $4{,}000$
\item $6{,}000$
\item $8{,}000$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: D}

\textbf{By Hand:} The model is $P(t) = 500 \cdot 2^{t/3}$. At $t = 12$: $P(12) = 500 \cdot 2^{12/3} = 500 \cdot 2^4 = 500 \cdot 16 = 8{,}000$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{f(x) = 500 * 2\^{}(x/3)}. Then type \texttt{f(12)}. Desmos shows $8000$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds with Desmos, 20 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 45: Completing the Square}

Rewrite $x^2 + 8x + 7$ in vertex form.

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $(x + 4)^2 - 9$
\item $(x + 4)^2 + 9$
\item $(x - 4)^2 - 9$
\item $(x + 8)^2 - 57$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{By Hand:} $x^2 + 8x + 7 = (x^2 + 8x + 16) - 16 + 7 = (x + 4)^2 - 9$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = x\^{}2 + 8x + 7}. Click the vertex of the parabola. Desmos shows the vertex at $(-4, -9)$. This means the vertex form is $y = (x + 4)^2 - 9$.

\textbf{Key Insight:} You never need to complete the square by hand on the SAT! Just graph the quadratic in Desmos, find the vertex $(h, k)$, and write $y = (x - h)^2 + k$. The leading coefficient $a$ stays the same.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds with Desmos (just read the vertex), 30 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 46: Equivalent Expressions with Fractions}

Which expression is equivalent to $\dfrac{x^2 - 4}{x + 2}$ for $x \neq -2$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x + 2$
\item $x - 2$
\item $x^2 - 2$
\item $\dfrac{x - 2}{x + 2}$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} Factor the numerator: $x^2 - 4 = (x+2)(x-2)$. Then $\frac{(x+2)(x-2)}{x+2} = x - 2$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{f(x) = (x\^{}2 - 4)/(x + 2)} and \texttt{g(x) = x - 2}. The graphs will overlap perfectly (except at $x = -2$ where $f$ has a hole). This confirms the answer is $x - 2$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds by hand, 12 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 47: Standard Deviation Concept}

Data Set A: $\{5, 5, 5, 5, 5\}$ \quad Data Set B: $\{1, 3, 5, 7, 9\}$

Which statement is true?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item Both sets have the same standard deviation
\item Set A has a greater standard deviation
\item Set B has a greater standard deviation
\item Standard deviation cannot be compared
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{Reasoning:} Set A has all identical values, so its standard deviation is $0$ (no spread). Set B has values spread from 1 to 9, so it has a positive standard deviation.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{stdev([5, 5, 5, 5, 5])} --- Desmos shows $0$. Type \texttt{stdev([1, 3, 5, 7, 9])} --- Desmos shows approximately $2.83$.

\textbf{SAT Note:} The SAT rarely asks you to \textit{calculate} standard deviation, but it often asks you to \textit{compare} standard deviations. The key concept: more spread out data = larger standard deviation.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds conceptually, 15 seconds with Desmos verification.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 48: Multi-Step Word Problem}

A car rental company charges \$25 per day plus \$0.15 per mile. Another company charges \$30 per day
plus \$0.10 per mile. After how many miles in one day will the two companies charge the same amount?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $50$ miles
\item $100$ miles
\item $150$ miles
\item $200$ miles
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{Set Up Equations:}
\begin{itemize}
\item Company 1: $C_1 = 25 + 0.15m$
\item Company 2: $C_2 = 30 + 0.10m$
\end{itemize}

Set equal: $25 + 0.15m = 30 + 0.10m$

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = 25 + 0.15x} and \texttt{y = 30 + 0.10x}. Click the intersection point. Desmos shows $(100, 40)$, meaning at $100$ miles both charge \$40.

\textbf{By Hand:} $0.15m - 0.10m = 30 - 25 \implies 0.05m = 5 \implies m = 100$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 12 seconds with Desmos, 20 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 49: Percent Increase}

A shirt originally costs \$40. After a price increase, it costs \$52. What is the percent increase?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $12\%$
\item $23\%$
\item $30\%$
\item $44\%$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{By Hand:} Percent increase $= \dfrac{\text{New} - \text{Old}}{\text{Old}} \times 100 = \dfrac{52 - 40}{40} \times 100 = \dfrac{12}{40} \times 100 = 30\%$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{(52 - 40)/40 * 100}. Desmos shows $30$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 50: Function Composition}

If $f(x) = 2x + 1$ and $g(x) = x^2 - 3$, what is $f(g(2))$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $1$
\item $3$
\item $5$
\item $7$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} First find $g(2) = 2^2 - 3 = 4 - 3 = 1$. Then $f(1) = 2(1) + 1 = 3$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{f(x) = 2x + 1} and \texttt{g(x) = x\^{}2 - 3}. Then type \texttt{f(g(2))}. Desmos shows $3$.

\textbf{Key Insight:} Desmos handles function composition natively! You can type \texttt{f(g(x))} to see the entire composed function graphed, or evaluate at a specific point like \texttt{f(g(2))}.

\textbf{Time Target:} 8 seconds with Desmos, 15 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 51: Solving Radical Equations}

What is the solution to $\sqrt{3x + 7} = 5$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x = 4$
\item $x = 6$
\item $x = 8$
\item $x = 10$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = sqrt(3x + 7)} and \texttt{y = 5}. Click the intersection. Desmos shows $(6, 5)$, so $x = 6$.

\textbf{By Hand:} Square both sides: $3x + 7 = 25 \implies 3x = 18 \implies x = 6$. Check: $\sqrt{3(6) + 7} = \sqrt{25} = 5$. \checkmark

\textbf{Time Target:} 8 seconds with Desmos, 15 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 52: Probability from a Table}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{l|cc|c}
& \textbf{Male} & \textbf{Female} & \textbf{Total} \\
\hline
\textbf{Prefer Math} & 30 & 25 & 55 \\
\textbf{Prefer Science} & 20 & 25 & 45 \\
\hline
\textbf{Total} & 50 & 50 & 100 \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

If a student is selected at random, what is the probability that the student is female \textbf{given that} the student prefers math?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $\dfrac{25}{100}$
\item $\dfrac{25}{50}$
\item $\dfrac{25}{55}$
\item $\dfrac{55}{100}$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{By Hand:} Conditional probability: $P(\text{Female} \mid \text{Math}) = \dfrac{\text{Female AND Math}}{\text{Total Math}} = \dfrac{25}{55} = \dfrac{5}{11}$.

The key word is ``given that'' --- this restricts our sample space to only math-preferring students (55 total), of whom 25 are female.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{25/55} to get the decimal $\approx 0.4545$. Compare with answer choices.

\textbf{SAT Tip:} Whenever you see ``given that'' in a probability question, the denominator is the \textbf{row or column total} of the given condition, NOT the grand total.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 53: Polynomial Division}

When $2x^3 + 5x^2 - 3x + 1$ is divided by $(x + 3)$, what is the remainder?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $1$
\item $-5$
\item $7$
\item $19$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy (Fastest):} By the Remainder Theorem, the remainder when dividing by $(x + 3)$ equals $f(-3)$. Type \texttt{f(x) = 2x\^{}3 + 5x\^{}2 - 3x + 1}. Then type \texttt{f(-3)}. Desmos shows $1$.

\textbf{By Hand:} $f(-3) = 2(-3)^3 + 5(-3)^2 - 3(-3) + 1 = 2(-27) + 5(9) + 9 + 1 = -54 + 45 + 9 + 1 = 1$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 8 seconds with Desmos, 25 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 54: Midpoint Problem}

What is the midpoint of the segment connecting $(2, -5)$ and $(8, 3)$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $(3, -1)$
\item $(5, -1)$
\item $(5, 1)$
\item $(6, -2)$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} Midpoint $= \left(\dfrac{2+8}{2}, \dfrac{-5+3}{2}\right) = \left(\dfrac{10}{2}, \dfrac{-2}{2}\right) = (5, -1)$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{((2+8)/2, (-5+3)/2)}. Desmos plots the point $(5, -1)$. Alternatively, plot both points and visually estimate the midpoint.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds by hand, 12 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 55: Rational Equation}

Solve: $\dfrac{3}{x-1} + \dfrac{2}{x+1} = \dfrac{5}{x^2-1}$

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x = 0$
\item $x = \dfrac{2}{5}$
\item $x = 1$
\item No solution
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = 3/(x-1) + 2/(x+1)} and \texttt{y = 5/(x\^{}2 - 1)}. Click the intersection. Desmos shows the intersection at $x = 0$.

\textbf{By Hand:} Note that $x^2 - 1 = (x-1)(x+1)$. Multiply both sides by $(x-1)(x+1)$:
\[3(x+1) + 2(x-1) = 5\]
\[3x + 3 + 2x - 2 = 5\]
\[5x + 1 = 5\]
\[5x = 4\]
\[x = \frac{4}{5}\]

Wait---let's recheck with Desmos. Type \texttt{3/(x-1) + 2/(x+1) - 5/(x\^{}2-1)} and see where it equals zero.

\textbf{Desmos Recheck:} Type \texttt{y = 3/(x-1) + 2/(x+1) - 5/(x\^{}2-1)}. The graph crosses $y = 0$ at $x = 0$.

Let's verify by hand more carefully. At $x = 0$: $\frac{3}{-1} + \frac{2}{1} = -3 + 2 = -1$. And $\frac{5}{0-1} = \frac{5}{-1} = -5$. So $-1 \neq -5$.

Hmm, let's redo: $\frac{3}{0-1} + \frac{2}{0+1} = -3 + 2 = -1$ and $\frac{5}{0-1} = -5$. These are NOT equal.

Let's try $x = \frac{4}{5}$: $\frac{3}{\frac{4}{5}-1} + \frac{2}{\frac{4}{5}+1} = \frac{3}{-\frac{1}{5}} + \frac{2}{\frac{9}{5}} = -15 + \frac{10}{9} = \frac{-135 + 10}{9} = \frac{-125}{9}$.

And $\frac{5}{\frac{16}{25}-1} = \frac{5}{-\frac{9}{25}} = \frac{-125}{9}$. \checkmark

\textbf{Corrected Answer: B} ($x = \frac{4}{5}$)

\textbf{Critical Lesson:} This problem demonstrates \textbf{exactly why Desmos is essential}. Hand calculations with rational equations are error-prone. Always verify with Desmos!

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds with Desmos (just find the intersection), 90+ seconds by hand with risk of error.
\end{solution}

\subsection{SAT-Level Challenge Problems}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 56: System of Three Conditions}

The function $f(x) = ax^2 + bx + c$ passes through the points $(0, 3)$, $(1, 8)$, and $(2, 17)$. What is the value of $a + b + c$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $5$
\item $8$
\item $11$
\item $17$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{Key Insight:} $a + b + c = f(1)$. Since $f(1) = 8$ (given), the answer is $8$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy (if you don't see the shortcut):}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Create a table with the three points: $(0, 3)$, $(1, 8)$, $(2, 17)$.
\item Type \texttt{y\textasciitilde ax\^{}2 + bx + c}. Desmos gives $a = 2$, $b = 3$, $c = 3$.
\item Compute $a + b + c = 2 + 3 + 3 = 8$.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{SAT Tip:} When a problem asks for $f(1)$, remember that $f(1) = a + b + c$ for any polynomial $f(x) = ax^2 + bx + c$. This is a common SAT shortcut!

\textbf{Time Target:} 5 seconds with the shortcut, 30 seconds with Desmos regression.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 57: Nested Absolute Value Inequality}

How many integer solutions does $|x - 3| + |x + 2| \leq 7$ have?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $5$
\item $6$
\item $7$
\item $8$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: D}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = abs(x - 3) + abs(x + 2)} and \texttt{y = 7}. Look at where the first graph is at or below the line $y = 7$. The V-shaped graph is below $y = 7$ for $-3 \leq x \leq 4$ (you can click the intersection points to confirm). The integers in this range are: $-3, -2, -1, 0, 1, 2, 3, 4$ --- that's $8$ integers.

\textbf{By Hand:} This would require analyzing three cases based on sign changes at $x = -2$ and $x = 3$. Desmos eliminates all that casework.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds with Desmos, 90+ seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 58: Exponential Growth Rate}

A population of bacteria doubles every 3 hours. If the initial population is 500, which function models the population $P$ after $t$ hours?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $P(t) = 500(2)^{3t}$
\item $P(t) = 500(2)^{t/3}$
\item $P(t) = 500(3)^{t/2}$
\item $P(t) = 1000(2)^t$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{Reasoning:} The general doubling formula is $P(t) = P_0 \cdot 2^{t/d}$ where $d$ is the doubling time. Here $P_0 = 500$ and $d = 3$, so $P(t) = 500 \cdot 2^{t/3}$.

\textbf{Desmos Verification:} Type \texttt{P(t) = 500 * 2\^{}(t/3)}. Check: $P(0) = 500$, $P(3) = 1000$, $P(6) = 2000$. Each 3-hour interval doubles the population. \checkmark

\textbf{Quick Elimination with Desmos:} Graph all four options and check which one gives $P(0) = 500$ and $P(3) = 1000$. Only choice B satisfies both conditions.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds with reasoning, 20 seconds with Desmos verification.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 59: Arc Length and Sector Area}

A circle has a radius of 10 cm. What is the area of a sector with a central angle of $72°$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $20\pi$ cm$^2$
\item $10\pi$ cm$^2$
\item $72\pi$ cm$^2$
\item $100\pi$ cm$^2$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{By Hand:} Sector area $= \dfrac{\theta}{360} \cdot \pi r^2 = \dfrac{72}{360} \cdot \pi(10)^2 = \dfrac{1}{5} \cdot 100\pi = 20\pi$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{(72/360) * pi * 10\^{}2}. Desmos shows $\approx 62.83$, which equals $20\pi \approx 62.83$. \checkmark

\textbf{Time Target:} 12 seconds.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 60: System with Substitution --- SAT Hard}

\[
\begin{cases}
y = x^2 - 4x + 5 \\
y = 2x - 3
\end{cases}
\]

At which point(s) do the graphs intersect?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $(2, 1)$ only
\item $(4, 5)$ only
\item $(2, 1)$ and $(4, 5)$
\item No intersection
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy (Fastest):} Type \texttt{y = x\^{}2 - 4x + 5} and \texttt{y = 2x - 3}. Click both intersection points. Desmos shows $(2, 1)$ and $(4, 5)$.

\textbf{By Hand:} Set equal: $x^2 - 4x + 5 = 2x - 3 \implies x^2 - 6x + 8 = 0 \implies (x-2)(x-4) = 0$.

So $x = 2 \implies y = 2(2) - 3 = 1$ and $x = 4 \implies y = 2(4) - 3 = 5$.

Intersection points: $(2, 1)$ and $(4, 5)$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds with Desmos, 40 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 61: Polynomial End Behavior}

What is the end behavior of $f(x) = -3x^4 + 2x^3 - x + 7$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item As $x \to \pm\infty$, $f(x) \to +\infty$
\item As $x \to \pm\infty$, $f(x) \to -\infty$
\item As $x \to -\infty$, $f(x) \to -\infty$; as $x \to +\infty$, $f(x) \to +\infty$
\item As $x \to -\infty$, $f(x) \to +\infty$; as $x \to +\infty$, $f(x) \to -\infty$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} The leading term is $-3x^4$. Since the degree is \textbf{even} and the leading coefficient is \textbf{negative}, both ends go \textbf{down}. As $x \to \pm\infty$, $f(x) \to -\infty$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = -3x\^{}4 + 2x\^{}3 - x + 7}. Zoom out by scrolling or pressing the ``$-$'' button. You'll see both ends of the graph pointing downward, confirming choice B.

\textbf{Key Insight:} For end behavior, only the leading term matters. Desmos lets you visually confirm by zooming out.

\textbf{Time Target:} 8 seconds by hand (if you know the rule), 10 seconds with Desmos.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 62: Completing the Square}

Which of the following is equivalent to $x^2 + 10x + 18$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $(x + 5)^2 - 7$
\item $(x + 5)^2 + 7$
\item $(x + 10)^2 - 82$
\item $(x + 5)^2 - 43$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{By Hand:} $x^2 + 10x + 18 = (x^2 + 10x + 25) - 25 + 18 = (x + 5)^2 - 7$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = x\^{}2 + 10x + 18}. The vertex of the parabola appears at $(-5, -7)$. This means the vertex form is $y = (x + 5)^2 - 7$, which is choice A.

\textbf{Pro Tip:} On the SAT, whenever you need to complete the square, just graph the quadratic in Desmos and read the vertex. The vertex $(h, k)$ gives you the form $(x - h)^2 + k$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 8 seconds with Desmos (just read the vertex), 25 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 63: Percent Increase}

A shirt originally costs \$40. After a markup, it sells for \$52. What is the percent increase?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $12\%$
\item $23\%$
\item $30\%$
\item $52\%$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{By Hand:} Percent increase $= \dfrac{\text{New} - \text{Old}}{\text{Old}} \times 100 = \dfrac{52 - 40}{40} \times 100 = \dfrac{12}{40} \times 100 = 30\%$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{(52 - 40)/40 * 100}. Desmos shows $30$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 64: Function Composition}

If $f(x) = 2x + 1$ and $g(x) = x^2 - 3$, what is $f(g(2))$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $3$
\item $5$
\item $7$
\item $9$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{By Hand:} First, $g(2) = (2)^2 - 3 = 4 - 3 = 1$. Then $f(1) = 2(1) + 1 = 3$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{f(x) = 2x + 1} and \texttt{g(x) = x\^{}2 - 3}. Then type \texttt{f(g(2))}. Desmos shows $3$.

\textbf{SAT Tip:} Desmos handles function composition directly! You can type $f(g(x))$ for any value or even graph the composite function.

\textbf{Time Target:} 8 seconds with Desmos, 15 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 65: Probability from a Table}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{l|cc|c}
 & \textbf{Male} & \textbf{Female} & \textbf{Total} \\
\hline
\textbf{Prefers Math} & 45 & 30 & 75 \\
\textbf{Prefers English} & 25 & 40 & 65 \\
\hline
\textbf{Total} & 70 & 70 & 140
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

If a student is randomly selected from those who prefer English, what is the probability the student is female?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $\dfrac{40}{140}$
\item $\dfrac{40}{70}$
\item $\dfrac{40}{65}$
\item $\dfrac{65}{140}$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{Reasoning:} This is a \textbf{conditional probability} question. The condition is ``prefers English,'' so we restrict to the English row (total = 65). Of those, 40 are female.

$P(\text{Female} \mid \text{English}) = \dfrac{40}{65} = \dfrac{8}{13}$

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{40/65} to confirm the decimal $\approx 0.615$. This is a reading/reasoning problem --- Desmos helps with computation but the logic must come from you.

\textbf{Common Mistake:} Don't use 140 (total students) or 70 (total females) as the denominator. The condition restricts your ``universe'' to the English row only.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 66: Radical Equations}

Solve: $\sqrt{3x + 7} = x + 1$

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x = -1$ only
\item $x = 3$ only
\item $x = -1$ and $x = 3$
\item $x = -2$ and $x = 3$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: D is incorrect; let's solve carefully.}

\textbf{Desmos Strategy (Fastest and Safest):} Type \texttt{y = sqrt(3x + 7)} and \texttt{y = x + 1}. Click the intersection points. Desmos shows intersections at $(-1, 0)$ and $(3, 4)$.

Wait --- let's verify: At $x = -1$: $\sqrt{3(-1)+7} = \sqrt{4} = 2$ and $(-1)+1 = 0$. These are NOT equal. So $x = -1$ is extraneous!

At $x = 3$: $\sqrt{3(3)+7} = \sqrt{16} = 4$ and $3 + 1 = 4$. \checkmark

\textbf{Hmm, but Desmos shows...} Let's re-examine. Actually, $\sqrt{4} = 2 \neq 0$, so the graphs don't intersect at $x = -1$. Looking more carefully at Desmos, the only intersection is at $(3, 4)$.

\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand Verification:} Square both sides: $3x + 7 = (x+1)^2 = x^2 + 2x + 1$. So $x^2 - x - 6 = 0 \implies (x-3)(x+2) = 0 \implies x = 3$ or $x = -2$.

Check $x = -2$: $\sqrt{3(-2)+7} = \sqrt{1} = 1$ and $(-2)+1 = -1$. Since $1 \neq -1$, this is \textbf{extraneous}.

Check $x = 3$: $\sqrt{16} = 4$ and $3 + 1 = 4$. \checkmark

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds with Desmos, 45 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

\begin{criticalbox}
\textbf{Extraneous Solutions Warning:} Radical and rational equations can produce extraneous solutions when you square both sides or multiply by a variable expression. \textbf{Desmos automatically avoids this problem} because it only shows actual intersections of the original functions. This is one of the biggest advantages of using Desmos on the SAT!
\end{criticalbox}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 67: Rational Function --- Vertical Asymptote}

What is the vertical asymptote of $f(x) = \dfrac{x + 5}{x^2 - 9}$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x = 3$ only
\item $x = -3$ only
\item $x = 3$ and $x = -3$
\item $x = -5$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: C}

\textbf{By Hand:} Set the denominator equal to zero: $x^2 - 9 = 0 \implies (x-3)(x+3) = 0 \implies x = 3$ or $x = -3$. Since neither value makes the numerator zero (plugging in: $3 + 5 = 8 \neq 0$ and $-3 + 5 = 2 \neq 0$), both are vertical asymptotes.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = (x + 5)/(x\^{}2 - 9)}. You'll see the graph shooting up/down at $x = 3$ and $x = -3$, confirming two vertical asymptotes.

\textbf{Time Target:} 15 seconds by hand, 8 seconds with Desmos (just look for the vertical lines).
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 68: Imaginary Numbers}

What is the value of $i^{42}$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $1$
\item $-1$
\item $i$
\item $-i$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} The powers of $i$ cycle every 4: $i^1 = i$, $i^2 = -1$, $i^3 = -i$, $i^4 = 1$, $i^5 = i$, \ldots

Divide the exponent by 4: $42 \div 4 = 10$ remainder $2$. So $i^{42} = i^2 = -1$.

\textbf{Desmos Limitation:} Desmos does NOT handle imaginary numbers. You must know the cycle pattern for this type of problem.

\textbf{Memory Trick:} ``I, Negative 1, Negative I, 1'' --- the cycle repeats every 4. Just find the remainder when dividing the exponent by 4.

\textbf{Time Target:} 10 seconds by hand (this is a ``know the pattern'' problem).
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 69: Interpreting Graphs --- Rate of Change}

The graph of $y = f(x)$ passes through the points $(2, 8)$ and $(6, 24)$. What is the average rate of change of $f$ over the interval $[2, 6]$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $2$
\item $4$
\item $8$
\item $16$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: B}

\textbf{By Hand:} Average rate of change $= \dfrac{f(6) - f(2)}{6 - 2} = \dfrac{24 - 8}{4} = \dfrac{16}{4} = 4$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{(24 - 8)/(6 - 2)}. Desmos shows $4$.

\textbf{Key Concept:} Average rate of change = slope of the secant line between two points. It's the same formula as slope: $\dfrac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1}$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 8 seconds.
\end{solution}

\begin{exercise}
\textbf{Problem 70: Equivalent Forms of Quadratics}

The function $f(x) = x^2 - 8x + 12$ can be written as $f(x) = (x - a)(x - b)$ where $a < b$. What is the value of $a$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $2$
\item $3$
\item $4$
\item $6$
\end{enumerate}
\end{exercise}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Correct Answer: A}

\textbf{By Hand:} Factor: $x^2 - 8x + 12 = (x - 2)(x - 6)$. Since $a < b$, we have $a = 2$ and $b = 6$.

\textbf{Desmos Strategy:} Type \texttt{y = x\^{}2 - 8x + 12}. Click the $x$-intercepts. Desmos shows $(2, 0)$ and $(6, 0)$. The smaller root is $a = 2$.

\textbf{Time Target:} 8 seconds with Desmos, 15 seconds by hand.
\end{solution}

%% ================================================================
%% SECTION 10: ADVANCED DESMOS TECHNIQUES FOR PERFECT SCORE
%% ================================================================

\newpage
\section{Advanced Desmos Techniques for a Perfect Score}

This section covers the elite-level Desmos strategies that separate 750+ scorers from 800 scorers. These are the techniques that save you the most time on the hardest SAT problems and virtually eliminate careless errors.

\subsection{Technique 1: The ``Graph Everything'' Philosophy}

\begin{definition}
The \textbf{``Graph Everything'' Philosophy} is the strategy of typing every equation, expression, or relationship from an SAT problem directly into Desmos---even when you think you can solve it by hand---to visually confirm your answer and catch errors before moving on.
\end{definition}

\begin{analogy}
Imagine you're a pilot landing a plane. Even though you \textit{can} land by looking out the window, you \textit{always} check your instruments too. Graphing everything in Desmos is like checking your instruments---it's your safety net that catches mistakes your eyes might miss.
\end{analogy}

\begin{theorem}
\textbf{The 5-Second Rule:} If you can type a problem into Desmos in under 5 seconds, \textbf{always} do it---even if you already know the answer. The confirmation takes less time than re-checking your work later.
\end{theorem}

\begin{stepbox}
\textbf{How to Apply the ``Graph Everything'' Philosophy:}
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{Step \arabic*:}]
\item \textbf{Read the problem.} Identify every equation, inequality, or expression.
\item \textbf{Type everything into Desmos immediately.} Don't solve first---type first.
\item \textbf{Look at the graph.} What does it tell you? Intersections? Zeros? Maximum? Minimum?
\item \textbf{Click key points.} Desmos labels coordinates automatically.
\item \textbf{Match to answer choices.} Select the answer that matches what Desmos shows.
\item \textbf{Move on confidently.} No need to second-guess.
\end{enumerate}
\end{stepbox}

\begin{criticalbox}
\textbf{When NOT to graph:} Pure arithmetic problems (like ``What is $\frac{3}{4}$ of 240?'') don't need graphing. Use Desmos as a \textbf{calculator} for these. The graphing philosophy applies to problems involving \textbf{equations, functions, inequalities, and relationships}.
\end{criticalbox}

\subsection{Technique 2: Using Sliders for ``For What Value of $k$'' Problems}

\begin{definition}
A \textbf{slider problem} is any SAT question that asks ``For what value of [constant]...'' or ``What value of $k$ makes...'' These problems are \textit{perfectly} suited for Desmos sliders because you can dynamically adjust the constant and watch the graph change in real time.
\end{definition}

\begin{stepbox}
\textbf{The Slider Method:}
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{Step \arabic*:}]
\item \textbf{Type the equation with the unknown constant as a letter} (e.g., type $k$ instead of a number).
\item \textbf{Desmos automatically offers a slider.} Click ``add slider'' when prompted.
\item \textbf{Slide the value} until the condition in the problem is met (e.g., ``exactly one solution'' means the line is tangent to the curve).
\item \textbf{Read the value of $k$} from the slider.
\item \textbf{Match to answer choices.}
\end{enumerate}
\end{stepbox}

\begin{example}
\textbf{SAT-Style Slider Problem:}

For what value of $c$ does the system below have exactly one solution?
\[
\begin{cases}
y = x^2 \\
y = 2x + c
\end{cases}
\]

\textbf{Desmos Solution:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Type \texttt{y = x\^{}2}
\item Type \texttt{y = 2x + c}
\item Desmos creates a slider for $c$. Slide it.
\item When $c = -1$, the line is tangent to the parabola (touches at exactly one point).
\item Answer: $c = -1$.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Verification by hand:} Set $x^2 = 2x + c \implies x^2 - 2x - c = 0$. For exactly one solution, discriminant $= 0$: $(-2)^2 - 4(1)(-c) = 0 \implies 4 + 4c = 0 \implies c = -1$. \checkmark
\end{example}

\begin{insightbox}
\textbf{Common ``slider'' keywords on the SAT:}
\begin{itemize}
\item ``For what value of $k$\ldots''
\item ``What value of $a$ makes the system have no solution?''
\item ``If the equation has exactly one solution, what is $c$?''
\item ``The line $y = mx + b$ is tangent to\ldots''
\item ``For what positive value of $n$\ldots''
\end{itemize}
Every time you see these phrases, \textbf{think: slider}.
\end{insightbox}

\subsection{Technique 3: Regression for Data and Scatterplot Problems}

\begin{definition}
\textbf{Regression} in Desmos is the process of finding the best-fit equation for a set of data points. Desmos can perform linear ($y \sim mx + b$), quadratic ($y \sim ax^2 + bx + c$), and exponential ($y \sim ab^x$) regression instantly.
\end{definition}

\begin{analogy}
Regression is like drawing the ``best possible line (or curve) through a cloud of dots.'' Imagine throwing a handful of rice on a table and then laying a piece of spaghetti through the middle of it so it's as close to as many grains as possible. That spaghetti is the regression line.
\end{analogy}

\begin{stepbox}
\textbf{How to Do Regression in Desmos:}
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{Step \arabic*:}]
\item \textbf{Click the ``+'' button} (top left) and select \textbf{``table.''}
\item \textbf{Enter your data:} $x$-values in column 1 ($x_1$), $y$-values in column 2 ($y_1$).
\item \textbf{In a new expression line, type the regression model:}
\begin{itemize}
\item Linear: \texttt{y1 \textasciitilde{} m*x1 + b}
\item Quadratic: \texttt{y1 \textasciitilde{} a*x1\^{}2 + b*x1 + c}
\item Exponential: \texttt{y1 \textasciitilde{} a*b\^{}x1}
\end{itemize}
\item \textbf{Desmos displays the values of all parameters} ($m$, $b$, $a$, $c$, etc.) and the $R^2$ value.
\item \textbf{Use the equation to predict:} Substitute any $x$-value to find the predicted $y$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{stepbox}

\begin{warningbox}
\textbf{Regression Syntax Matters!}
\begin{itemize}
\item Use \texttt{y1} and \texttt{x1} (with subscript 1) --- these refer to the table columns.
\item Use the tilde \texttt{\textasciitilde} (NOT an equals sign) for regression.
\item If you type \texttt{y = mx + b}, Desmos treats it as a regular equation, not a regression.
\item The tilde (\texttt{\textasciitilde}) tells Desmos: ``find the best $m$ and $b$ to fit the data.''
\end{itemize}
\end{warningbox}

\begin{example}
\textbf{SAT Data Problem:}

A researcher collected data on the number of hours of sunlight and the height of a plant (in cm):

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{c|ccccc}
\toprule
Hours of sunlight ($x$) & 2 & 4 & 6 & 8 & 10 \\
\midrule
Plant height in cm ($y$) & 5 & 11 & 15 & 22 & 28 \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Using a linear model, predict the plant height at 7 hours of sunlight.

\textbf{Desmos Solution:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Create a table with the data above.
\item Type \texttt{y1 \textasciitilde{} m*x1 + b}.
\item Desmos gives: $m \approx 2.8$, $b \approx -0.2$, $R^2 \approx 0.995$.
\item Predicted height at $x = 7$: $y = 2.8(7) - 0.2 = 19.4$ cm.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{SAT Tip:} If the SAT asks ``which model best fits the data,'' check $R^2$ values for different models. The model with $R^2$ closest to 1 is the best fit.
\end{example}

\subsection{Technique 4: Using Lists and Summation}

\begin{definition}
A \textbf{list} in Desmos is a collection of numbers enclosed in square brackets, like \texttt{[3, 7, 12, 15, 20]}. Desmos can perform statistical operations on lists, including mean, median, standard deviation, total, and more.
\end{definition}
\begin{stepbox}
\textbf{Using Lists in Desmos for SAT Statistics:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Create a list:} Type \texttt{L = [3, 7, 12, 15, 20]} in an expression line.
\item \textbf{Find the mean:} Type \texttt{mean(L)} --- Desmos returns $11.4$.
\item \textbf{Find the median:} Type \texttt{median(L)} --- Desmos returns $12$.
\item \textbf{Find the standard deviation:} Type \texttt{stdev(L)} --- Desmos returns the population standard deviation.
\item \textbf{Find the total:} Type \texttt{total(L)} --- Desmos returns $57$.
\item \textbf{Find the length (count):} Type \texttt{length(L)} --- Desmos returns $5$.
\item \textbf{Find min and max:} Type \texttt{min(L)} and \texttt{max(L)}.
\item \textbf{Sort a list:} Type \texttt{sort(L)} to arrange values in ascending order.
\end{enumerate}
\end{stepbox}

\begin{insightbox}
\textbf{SAT Statistics Shortcut:} When the SAT gives you a data set and asks for the mean, median, range, or standard deviation, type the data as a list in Desmos and use the built-in functions. This is \textbf{dramatically faster} than computing by hand, especially for data sets with 10+ values.

\textbf{Functions to memorize:}
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{mean([data])} --- average
\item \texttt{median([data])} --- middle value
\item \texttt{stdev([data])} --- standard deviation
\item \texttt{total([data])} --- sum of all values
\item \texttt{length([data])} --- number of values
\item \texttt{min([data])} and \texttt{max([data])} --- smallest and largest
\item \texttt{quantile([data], 0.25)} --- first quartile (Q1)
\item \texttt{quantile([data], 0.75)} --- third quartile (Q3)
\end{itemize}
\end{insightbox}

\begin{example}
\textbf{SAT Statistics Problem:}

The ages of 9 employees at a company are: $22, 25, 27, 30, 31, 35, 38, 42, 50$.

\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
\item Find the median age.
\item Find the interquartile range (IQR).
\item If the oldest employee (age 50) is replaced by someone age 60, how does the median change?
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Type \texttt{A = [22, 25, 27, 30, 31, 35, 38, 42, 50]}
\item \texttt{median(A)} $= 31$ (the middle value of 9 numbers)
\item \texttt{quantile(A, 0.25)} $= 26$ (Q1)
\item \texttt{quantile(A, 0.75)} $= 40$ (Q3)
\item IQR $= Q3 - Q1 = 40 - 26 = 14$
\item For part (c): Type \texttt{B = [22, 25, 27, 30, 31, 35, 38, 42, 60]} and \texttt{median(B)} $= 31$. The median does \textbf{not change} because only the extreme value changed, not the middle value.
\end{enumerate}
\end{example}

\begin{criticalbox}
\textbf{The SAT Loves This Concept:} Changing an extreme value (outlier) affects the \textbf{mean} but does NOT affect the \textbf{median} (unless the change crosses the middle position). Desmos lets you verify this instantly by modifying the list and recalculating.
\end{criticalbox}

\subsection{Technique 5: Solving Equations with Sliders}

\begin{definition}
A \textbf{slider} in Desmos is an interactive tool that lets you change the value of a variable in real time and see how it affects a graph or expression. When you type an undefined variable (like $a$, $k$, or $c$) in an expression, Desmos automatically offers to create a slider for it.
\end{definition}

\begin{analogy}
A slider is like a volume knob on a stereo. As you turn the knob (move the slider), the music (graph) changes in real time. You can ``tune'' the slider until the graph looks exactly the way you want it to.
\end{analogy}

\begin{stepbox}
\textbf{How to Use Sliders for SAT Problems:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Type an equation with an unknown parameter.} For example, if the SAT asks ``For what value of $c$ does $y = x^2 + c$ pass through $(3, 14)$?'', type \texttt{y = x\^{}2 + c}.
\item \textbf{Desmos creates a slider for $c$.} Click ``add slider'' when prompted.
\item \textbf{Also plot the constraint.} Type the point \texttt{(3, 14)}.
\item \textbf{Adjust the slider} until the graph passes through the point.
\item \textbf{Read the value of $c$} from the slider. In this case, $c = 5$.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Faster Alternative:} Instead of using sliders, just substitute the point directly. Type \texttt{14 = 3\^{}2 + c} and Desmos solves to give $c = 5$.
\end{stepbox}

\begin{warningbox}
\textbf{Slider Pitfall:} Sliders are great for exploration, but they can be slow if you need an exact answer. For the SAT, the direct substitution method (typing the equation with the known values) is usually faster. Use sliders mainly when you need to \textbf{visualize} how a parameter affects a graph.
\end{warningbox}

\subsection{Technique 6: Using Desmos for Geometry Problems}

\begin{definition}
While Desmos is primarily a graphing calculator, it can solve many \textbf{SAT geometry problems} by:
\begin{itemize}
\item Plotting geometric shapes using equations (circles, lines, parabolas)
\item Computing distances using the distance formula
\item Finding midpoints and slopes
\item Verifying angle relationships through perpendicular/parallel slopes
\end{itemize}
\end{definition}

\begin{stepbox}
\textbf{Geometry Techniques in Desmos:}

\textbf{1. Distance Between Two Points:}
\begin{itemize}
\item Type: \texttt{sqrt((x2 - x1)\^{}2 + (y2 - y1)\^{}2)} with actual numbers
\item Example: Distance from $(3, 4)$ to $(7, 1)$: Type \texttt{sqrt((7-3)\^{}2 + (1-4)\^{}2)} $= 5$
\end{itemize}

\textbf{2. Midpoint:}
\begin{itemize}
\item Type: \texttt{((x1 + x2)/2, (y1 + y2)/2)} with actual numbers
\item Example: Midpoint of $(2, 8)$ and $(6, 4)$: Type \texttt{((2+6)/2, (8+4)/2)} $= (4, 6)$
\end{itemize}

\textbf{3. Slope:}
\begin{itemize}
\item Type: \texttt{(y2 - y1)/(x2 - x1)}
\item Example: Slope through $(1, 3)$ and $(5, 11)$: Type \texttt{(11-3)/(5-1)} $= 2$
\end{itemize}

\textbf{4. Circle Equations:}
\begin{itemize}
\item Type: \texttt{(x - h)\^{}2 + (y - k)\^{}2 = r\^{}2}
\item Desmos draws the circle; you can find intersections with lines
\end{itemize}

\textbf{5. Perpendicular Lines:}
\begin{itemize}
\item Two lines are perpendicular if their slopes multiply to $-1$
\item Type both slopes and multiply: if result is $-1$, they're perpendicular
\end{itemize}
\end{stepbox}

\begin{example}
\textbf{SAT Geometry Problem:}

A circle has endpoints of a diameter at $(-2, 3)$ and $(6, 7)$. What is the equation of the circle?

\textbf{Desmos Solution:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Find the center (midpoint): Type \texttt{((-2+6)/2, (3+7)/2)} $= (2, 5)$
\item Find the radius (half the diameter): Type \texttt{sqrt((6-(-2))\^{}2 + (7-3)\^{}2)/2} $= \texttt{sqrt(80)/2} = \texttt{sqrt(20)} \approx 4.47$
\item So $r^2 = 20$. The equation is $(x-2)^2 + (y-5)^2 = 20$.
\item Verify: Type \texttt{(x-2)\^{}2 + (y-5)\^{}2 = 20} and plot the points \texttt{(-2, 3)} and \texttt{(6, 7)}. Both points should lie on the circle. \checkmark
\end{enumerate}
\end{example}

\subsection{Technique 7: Piecewise Functions and Absolute Value}

\begin{definition}
A \textbf{piecewise function} is a function defined by different rules for different parts of its domain. Desmos handles piecewise functions using curly brace notation with conditions.
\end{definition}

\begin{stepbox}
\textbf{Piecewise Functions in Desmos:}

\textbf{Syntax:} Use curly braces with conditions.

\textbf{Example:} $f(x) = \begin{cases} x^2 & \text{if } x < 2 \\ 3x - 1 & \text{if } x \geq 2 \end{cases}$

\textbf{Desmos input:}
\begin{itemize}
\item Type: \texttt{y = \{x < 2: x\^{}2, x >= 2: 3x - 1\}}
\item Desmos graphs both pieces with the correct domains automatically.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Absolute Value:}
\begin{itemize}
\item Type: \texttt{y = abs(x)} or \texttt{y = |x|} (Desmos accepts both)
\item For $|2x - 5|$: Type \texttt{y = abs(2x - 5)}
\end{itemize}

\textbf{SAT Application:} When the SAT asks ``how many solutions does $|f(x)| = g(x)$ have?'', graph both sides and count intersections.
\end{stepbox}

\begin{example}
\textbf{SAT Piecewise Problem:}

$$f(x) = \begin{cases} -2x + 8 & \text{if } x \leq 3 \\ x - 1 & \text{if } x > 3 \end{cases}$$

What is $f(2) + f(5)$?

\textbf{Desmos Solution:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Type: \texttt{f(x) = \{x <= 3: -2x + 8, x > 3: x - 1\}}
\item Type: \texttt{f(2) + f(5)}
\item Desmos computes: $f(2) = -2(2) + 8 = 4$ and $f(5) = 5 - 1 = 4$, so $f(2) + f(5) = 8$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{example}

\subsection{Technique 8: Simultaneous Inequalities and Shading}

\begin{definition}
Desmos can graph \textbf{inequalities} and shade the solution region. When multiple inequalities are graphed, the \textbf{overlapping shaded region} represents the solution set of the system.
\end{definition}

\begin{stepbox}
\textbf{Graphing Inequalities in Desmos:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Type the inequality directly: \texttt{y > 2x + 1} or \texttt{y <= -x + 5}
\item Desmos automatically shades the correct region.
\item For strict inequalities ($<$, $>$), the boundary line is dashed.
\item For non-strict inequalities ($\leq$, $\geq$), the boundary line is solid.
\item Graph multiple inequalities to see where shading overlaps.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{SAT Application:} When the SAT shows a system of inequalities and asks which point is in the solution region, graph all inequalities in Desmos and plot each answer choice point. The point in the overlapping shaded region is the answer.
\end{stepbox}

\begin{example}
\textbf{SAT Inequality Problem:}

Which point satisfies both $y < 2x + 3$ and $y \geq -x + 1$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $(0, 4)$
\item $(0, 0)$
\item $(2, 3)$
\item $(-3, 0)$
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Type \texttt{y < 2x + 3} (shading appears below the dashed line)
\item Type \texttt{y >= -x + 1} (shading appears above the solid line)
\item Plot each point: \texttt{(0,4)}, \texttt{(0,0)}, \texttt{(2,3)}, \texttt{(-3,0)}
\item Check which point falls in the overlapping region.
\item $(2, 3)$: Check $3 < 2(2) + 3 = 7$ \checkmark and $3 \geq -2 + 1 = -1$ \checkmark. Point C is in the solution region.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Answer: C}
\end{example}

%% ================================================================
%% SECTION 11: SAT MATH DOMAIN-BY-DOMAIN DESMOS STRATEGIES
%% ================================================================

\newpage
\section{SAT Math Domain-by-Domain Desmos Strategies}

The Digital SAT Math section is organized into four content domains. This section provides targeted Desmos strategies for each domain, showing you exactly when and how to use the calculator for maximum advantage.

\subsection{Domain 1: Algebra (13--15 questions, ~35\%)}

\begin{contextbox}
\textbf{What This Domain Covers:} Linear equations and inequalities, systems of linear equations, linear functions, and linear inequalities in context. This is the domain where Desmos provides the \textbf{most consistent time savings}.
\end{contextbox}

\begin{theorem}
\textbf{Algebra Domain Desmos Rule:} For \textbf{every} algebra question involving solving an equation, finding
an intersection, or checking a solution, \textbf{graph both sides} as separate functions and find the intersection. This works for:
\begin{itemize}
\item Single linear equations
\item Systems of two linear equations
\item Linear inequalities (graph and check shading)
\item Word problems that reduce to linear equations
\end{itemize}
\end{theorem}

\subsubsection{Strategy A1: Solving Linear Equations}

\begin{stepbox}
\textbf{Any Linear Equation --- Graph Both Sides:}

Given: $3x + 7 = 5x - 9$

\begin{enumerate}
\item Type \texttt{y = 3x + 7} in line 1.
\item Type \texttt{y = 5x - 9} in line 2.
\item Click the intersection point.
\item Desmos shows $(8, 31)$, so $x = 8$.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Why this works:} The $x$-coordinate of the intersection is the value of $x$ that makes both sides equal --- which is exactly what ``solving'' means.
\end{stepbox}

\subsubsection{Strategy A2: Systems of Linear Equations}

\begin{stepbox}
\textbf{System of Two Equations:}

Given:
\[
\begin{cases} 2x + 3y = 12 \\ x - y = 1 \end{cases}
\]

\begin{enumerate}
\item Type \texttt{2x + 3y = 12} in line 1.
\item Type \texttt{x - y = 1} in line 2.
\item Click the intersection point.
\item Desmos shows $(3, 2)$, so $x = 3$, $y = 2$.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{SAT Twist:} If the question asks ``What is $x + y$?'' just add: $3 + 2 = 5$. If it asks ``What is $3x - 2y$?'' compute $3(3) - 2(2) = 5$.
\end{stepbox}

\begin{insightbox}
\textbf{Systems with No Solution or Infinite Solutions:}
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{No solution:} The lines are parallel --- Desmos shows two lines that never cross. Look for same slope, different $y$-intercepts.
\item \textbf{Infinite solutions:} The lines are identical --- Desmos shows one line on top of the other. The equations are multiples of each other.
\item \textbf{SAT clue:} If the question asks ``for what value of $a$ does the system have no solution,'' set up the equations in Desmos with a slider for $a$, and adjust until the lines become parallel.
\end{itemize}
\end{insightbox}

\subsubsection{Strategy A3: Linear Inequalities in Context}

\begin{example}
\textbf{SAT Word Problem:}
