\newpage
\section{The Ultimate SAT Desmos Cheat Sheet}

\begin{criticalbox}
\textbf{PRINT THIS SECTION AND REVIEW IT BEFORE EVERY PRACTICE TEST.}

This is your one-page mental reference for Desmos strategies on the Digital SAT. Internalize these patterns and you will save 5--10 minutes on every math module.
\end{criticalbox}

\subsection{Quick-Reference: What to Type for Every Problem Type}

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.6}
\begin{longtable}{>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{3.8cm} >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{4.5cm} >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{4.5cm}}
\toprule
\textbf{Problem Type} & \textbf{What to Type in Desmos} & \textbf{What to Look For} \\
\midrule
\endfirsthead
\toprule
\textbf{Problem Type} & \textbf
{What to Type in Desmos} & \textbf{What to Look For} \\
\midrule
\endhead
\midrule
\multicolumn{3}{r}{\textit{Continued on next page\ldots}} \\
\bottomrule
\endfoot
\bottomrule
\endlastfoot

Solve equation $f(x) = 0$ & \texttt{y = [expression]} & $x$-intercepts (click the dots) \\

Solve $f(x) = g(x)$ & \texttt{y = f(x)} and \texttt{y = g(x)} on separate lines & Intersection points (click them) \\

System of linear equations & Type both equations & Intersection point \\

Find vertex of parabola & \texttt{y = ax\^{}2 + bx + c} & Click the max/min point \\

Find $x$-intercepts & \texttt{y = [expression]} & Click where graph crosses $x$-axis \\

Find $y$-intercept & \texttt{y = [expression]} & Click where graph crosses $y$-axis; or type \texttt{f(0)} \\

Evaluate $f(a)$ & \texttt{f(x) = [expression]} then type \texttt{f(a)} & Read the number output \\

Composition $f(g(a))$ & Define both functions, type \texttt{f(g(a))} & Read the number output \\

Linear regression & Enter data in table, type \texttt{y1 \textasciitilde{} mx1 + b} & Read $m$ and $b$ values \\

Exponential regression & Enter data in table, type \texttt{y1 \textasciitilde{} a $\cdot$ b\^{}x1} & Read $a$ and $b$ values \\

Quadratic regression & Enter data in table, type \texttt{y1 \textasciitilde{} ax1\^{}2 + bx1 + c} & Read $a$, $b$, $c$ values \\

Number of solutions & Graph both sides of equation & Count intersection points \\

No solution system & Graph both lines & Parallel lines (no intersection) \\

Infinite solutions & Graph both lines & Lines overlap completely \\

Domain restrictions & \texttt{y = [expression]} & Look for gaps, asymptotes, holes \\

Absolute value equation & \texttt{y = |expression|} and \texttt{y = k} & Count/find intersections \\

Inequality solution & Type inequality directly (e.g., \texttt{2x + 3 > 7}) & Shaded region on number line \\

System of inequalities & Type both inequalities & Overlapping shaded region \\

Circle equation & Type equation directly & Circle appears; click for center/radius \\

Exponential growth/decay & \texttt{y = a $\cdot$ b\^{}x} & Read specific values by clicking \\

Minimum/maximum value & Graph the function & Click the highest or lowest point \\

Equivalent expressions & Graph original and each choice & Graphs that overlap perfectly \\

Percent change & Type calculation directly & Read the number \\

Arithmetic with fractions & Type the fraction expression & Exact decimal or fraction output \\

Distance formula & \texttt{sqrt((x2-x1)\^{}2 + (y2-y1)\^{}2)} & Read the distance \\

Midpoint & \texttt{((x1+x2)/2, (y1+y2)/2)} & Read the coordinates \\

Slope between two points & \texttt{(y2-y1)/(x2-x1)} & Read the slope value \\

\end{longtable}
\end{center}

\subsection{The 10 Commandments of SAT Desmos}

\begin{criticalbox}
\textbf{Memorize These 10 Rules:}

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{\arabic*.}]
\item \textbf{Thou shalt always graph both sides.} When solving $f(x) = g(x)$, put each side on its own line and find the intersection.

\item \textbf{Thou shalt click on points of interest.} Never eyeball coordinates. Always click directly on intercepts, vertices, and intersections for exact values.

\item \textbf{Thou shalt use sliders for unknowns.} When a problem has a parameter ($a$, $b$, $k$, etc.), let Desmos create a slider and adjust it to match the given condition.

\item \textbf{Thou shalt use tables for data.} Whenever a problem gives you data points, enter them in a Desmos table and use regression.

\item \textbf{Thou shalt test answer choices.} When stuck, substitute each answer choice and see which one works.

\item \textbf{Thou shalt zoom and adjust.} If you cannot see the important part of the graph, use pinch-to-zoom or click the wrench icon to adjust the viewing window.

\item \textbf{Thou shalt use parentheses religiously.} Every fraction numerator, every exponent base, every negative sign --- wrap them in parentheses.

\item \textbf{Thou shalt define functions with $f(x)$ notation.} This lets you evaluate $f(3)$, $f(-2)$, $f(g(x))$, etc. directly.

\item \textbf{Thou shalt not waste time on algebra Desmos can do.} If it involves computation, graphing, or equation solving, let Desmos handle it.

\item \textbf{Thou shalt practice before test day.} Desmos speed comes from muscle memory. Practice at \texttt{desmos.com/calculator} until every technique is automatic.
\end{enumerate}
\end{criticalbox}

\subsection{Speed Benchmarks: How Fast You Should Be}

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.5}
\begin{tabular}{>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{5.5cm} c c}
\toprule
\textbf{Desmos Action} & \textbf{Target Time} & \textbf{Beginner Time} \\
\midrule
Type a linear equation and find intercept & 10 sec & 25 sec \\
Type a quadratic and find vertex & 15 sec & 35 sec \\
Set up a system and find intersection & 15 sec & 40 sec \\
Enter 5 data points in a table & 20 sec & 50 sec \\
Run a regression and read parameters & 10 sec & 30 sec \\
Create a slider and adjust to match condition & 15 sec & 45 sec \\
Test all 4 answer choices by substitution & 20 sec & 60 sec \\
Graph an inequality and identify solution region & 10 sec & 30 sec \\
Graph a circle and identify center/radius & 10 sec & 25 sec \\
Evaluate a composition $f(g(3))$ & 10 sec & 30 sec \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\begin{insightbox}
\textbf{The 30-Second Rule:}

If you cannot set up the Desmos approach within 30 seconds, switch to solving by hand or try a different Desmos strategy. The goal is efficiency --- Desmos should \textbf{save} time, not consume it while you figure out how to use it.
\end{insightbox}

\subsection{Keyboard and Interface Shortcuts}

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabular}{>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{4cm} >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{8.5cm}}
\toprule
\textbf{Shortcut / Action} & \textbf{How to Do It} \\
\midrule
Exponents & Type \texttt{\^{}} then the power (e.g., \texttt{x\^{}2}) \\
Fractions & Type \texttt{/} (e.g., \texttt{3/4} displays as $\frac{3}{4}$) \\
Square root & Type \texttt{sqrt} (e.g., \texttt{sqrt(25)}) \\
$n$th root & Type \texttt{nthroot} \\
Absolute value & Type \texttt{|} on both sides (e.g., \texttt{|x-3|}) \\
Pi ($\pi$) & Type \texttt{pi} \\
Subscripts & Type \texttt{\_} (e.g., \texttt{x\_1} for $x_1$) \\
Inequality symbols & Type \texttt{<}, \texttt{>}, \texttt{<=}, \texttt{>=} \\
Log base 10 & Type \texttt{log(x)} \\
Natural log & Type \texttt{ln(x)} \\
Log base $n$ & Type \texttt{log\_n(x)} (e.g., \texttt{log\_2(8)}) \\
Add a table & Click the \texttt{+} button, select ``Table'' \\
Add a slider & Type a letter not yet defined (Desmos prompts ``add slider'') \\
Zoom to fit & Click the home icon (magnifying glass with house) \\
Undo & \texttt{Ctrl+Z} (or \texttt{Cmd+Z} on Mac) \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\subsection{The Emergency Protocol: When You're Completely Stuck}

\begin{stepbox}
\textbf{If you have NO idea how to solve a problem, follow this emergency protocol:}

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{Step \arabic*:}]
\item \textbf{Read the question one more time.} Identify: What are they asking for? What information is given?

\item \textbf{Type everything you can into Desmos.} Any equation, expression, or number from the problem --- just get it on screen.

\item \textbf{Graph it.} Even if you are not sure what to do, seeing the graph often reveals the answer.

\item \textbf{Test the answer choices.} Substitute each one into the original equation or condition. One of them will work.

\item \textbf{Look for key features.} Intercepts, vertices, intersections, asymptotes --- click on anything that looks important.

\item \textbf{If all else fails, make an educated guess and move on.} Do NOT spend more than 90 seconds on any single problem. There is no penalty for guessing on the SAT.
\end{enumerate}
\end{stepbox}

\subsection{Summary: The Desmos Cheat Sheet Mental Model}

\begin{insightbox}
\textbf{Remember the Three Golden Questions:}

Before every SAT math problem, ask yourself:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Can I type this directly into Desmos?} $\rightarrow$ If yes, do it immediately.
\item \textbf{Can I graph both sides and find an intersection?} $\rightarrow$ If yes, graph and click.
\item \textbf{Can I test the answer choices?} $\rightarrow$ If yes, substitute and verify.
\end{enumerate}

If you can answer ``yes'' to any of these three questions, \textbf{Desmos will get you the answer faster than algebra.} That is the entire philosophy of this guide.
\end{insightbox}

%% ================================================================
%% SECTION 17: FULL SAT PRACTICE MODULE WITH DESMOS
%% ================================================================

\newpage
\section{Full SAT Practice Module with Desmos Solutions}

This section simulates a complete SAT Math module. For every problem, we provide the traditional solution AND the Desmos speed solution so you can compare approaches and see how much time Desmos saves.

\begin{contextbox}
\textbf{How to Use This Section:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item First, try each problem on your own with Desmos (time yourself).
\item Then read the Desmos solution to see if your method matched.
\item Finally, read the traditional solution to deepen your algebraic understanding.
\item Target: Complete all 22 problems in under 35 minutes using Desmos.
\end{enumerate}
\end{contextbox}

\subsection{Module Practice Problems}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 1 (Easy --- Algebra):}

If $3x + 7 = 22$, what is the value of $x$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $3$
\item $5$
\item $7$
\item $15$
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: B}

\textbf{
Desmos Solution:} Type \texttt{3x + 7 = 22} directly into Desmos. Desmos shows $x = 5$.

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} $3x + 7 = 22 \Rightarrow 3x = 15 \Rightarrow x = 5$.

\textbf{Time Comparison:} Desmos: 5 seconds. Algebra: 10 seconds. Both fast, but Desmos requires zero thought.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 2 (Easy --- Linear Equations):}

What is the slope of the line $4x - 2y = 10$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $-2$
\item $2$
\item $4$
\item $-5$
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:} Type \texttt{4x - 2y = 10} into Desmos. The line appears. Click on two points on the line, such as $(0, -5)$ and $(1, -3)$. Slope $= \frac{-3 - (-5)}{1 - 0} = \frac{2}{1} = 2$.

\textbf{Alternative Desmos Method:} Rearrange mentally or type \texttt{y = 2x - 5} and confirm the graphs overlap. The coefficient of $x$ is the slope: $2$.

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} $4x - 2y = 10 \Rightarrow -2y = -4x + 10 \Rightarrow y = 2x - 5$. Slope $= 2$.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 3 (Easy --- Percentages):}

A shirt originally costs \$40. It is on sale for 25\% off. What is the sale price?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $\$10$
\item $\$15$
\item $\$30$
\item $\$35$
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: C}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:} Type \texttt{40 - 0.25 * 40} into Desmos. Result: $30$. Or type \texttt{40 * (1 - 0.25)} which gives $30$.

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} $25\%$ of $\$40 = 0.25 \times 40 = \$10$ discount. Sale price $= 40 - 10 = \$30$.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 4 (Easy --- Function Evaluation):}

If $f(x) = x^2 - 3x + 5$, what is $f(4)$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $7$
\item $9$
\item $11$
\item $13$
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:} Type \texttt{f(x) = x\^{}2 - 3x + 5}, then type \texttt{f(4)}. Desmos instantly outputs $9$.

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} $f(4) = (4)^2 - 3(4) + 5 = 16 - 12 + 5 = 9$.

\textbf{Time Comparison:} Desmos: 8 seconds. Algebra: 15 seconds. Desmos eliminates arithmetic errors.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 5 (Easy --- Interpreting Graphs):}

The graph of a linear function passes through $(0, 3)$ and $(2, 9)$. What is the equation of the line?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $y = 3x + 3$
\item $y = 3x - 3$
\item $y = 6x + 3$
\item $y = 2x + 3$
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: A}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:} Enter a table with points $(0, 3)$ and $(2, 9)$. Type \texttt{y1 \textasciitilde{} mx1 + b}. Desmos gives $m = 3$, $b = 3$. Equation: $y = 3x + 3$.

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} Slope $= \frac{9-3}{2-0} = \frac{6}{2} = 3$. The $y$-intercept is $3$ (from the point $(0,3)$). So $y = 3x + 3$.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 6 (Medium --- Systems of Equations):}

What is the solution to the system?
\begin{align*}
y &= 2x + 1 \\
y &= -x + 7
\end{align*}

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $(1, 3)$
\item $(2, 5)$
\item $(3, 4)$
\item $(4, 3)$
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:} Type \texttt{y = 2x + 1} on line 1 and \texttt{y = -x + 7} on line 2. Click the intersection point. Desmos shows $(2, 5)$.

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} Set equal: $2x + 1 = -x + 7 \Rightarrow 3x = 6 \Rightarrow x = 2$. Then $y = 2(2) + 1 = 5$. Solution: $(2, 5)$.

\textbf{Time Comparison:} Desmos: 10 seconds. Algebra: 25 seconds.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 7 (Medium --- Quadratic Zeros):}

What are the solutions to $x^2 - 5x - 14 = 0$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $x = 7$ and $x = -2$
\item $x = -7$ and $x = 2$
\item $x = 7$ and $x = 2$
\item $x = -7$ and $x = -2$
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: A}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:} Type \texttt{y = x\^{}2 - 5x - 14}. Click the two $x$-intercepts. Desmos shows $x = 7$ and $x = -2$.

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} Factor: $x^2 - 5x - 14 = (x - 7)(x + 2) = 0$. So $x = 7$ or $x = -2$.

\textbf{Desmos Advantage:} Even if you can't factor, Desmos finds the roots instantly.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 8 (Medium --- Exponential Growth):}

A population starts at 200 and grows by 15\% each year. What is the population after 5 years, to the nearest whole number?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $350$
\item $402$
\item $450$
\item $575$
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:} Type \texttt{f(x) = 200 * 1.15\^{}x}, then type \texttt{f(5)}. Desmos outputs $402.271...$, which rounds to $402$.

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} $P = 200(1.15)^5 = 200(2.01136...) = 402.27... \approx 402$.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 9 (Medium --- Equivalent Expressions):}

Which expression is equivalent to $(3x + 2)(x - 4)$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $3x^2 - 10x - 8$
\item $3x^2 + 10x - 8$
\item $3x^2 - 12x - 8$
\item $3x^2 - 10x + 8$
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: A}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:} Type \texttt{f(x) = (3x + 2)(x - 4)} on line 1. Type each answer choice on subsequent lines. The graph that perfectly overlaps $f(x)$ is the answer. Choice A: \texttt{g(x) = 3x\^{}2 - 10x - 8} overlaps perfectly.

\textbf{Quick Numerical Check:} $f(0) = (2)(-4) = -8$ and $g(0) = 0 - 0 - 8 = -8$. $f(1) = (5)(-3) = -15$ and $g(1) = 3 - 10 - 8 = -15$. Match!

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} $(3x+2)(x-4) = 3x^2 - 12x + 2x - 8 = 3x^2 - 10x - 8$.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 10 (Medium --- Absolute Value):}

How many solutions does $|x - 3| = 2x + 1$ have?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $0$
\item $1$
\item $2$
\item $3$
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:} Type \texttt{y = abs(x - 3)} and \texttt{y = 2x + 1}. Count the intersection points. There is exactly $1$ intersection point (at approximately $x = 0.667$).

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} 

Case 1: $x - 3 = 2x + 1 \Rightarrow -4 = x$, so $x = -4$. Check: $|-4-3| = 7$ and $2(-4)+1 = -7$. Since $7 \neq -7$, this is extraneous.

Case 2: $-(x-3) = 2x + 1 \Rightarrow -x + 3 = 2x + 1 \Rightarrow 2 = 3x \Rightarrow x = \frac{2}{3}$. Check: $|\frac{2}{3} - 3| = \frac{7}{3}$ and $2(\frac{2}{3}) + 1 = \frac{7}{3}$. Valid! One solution.

\textbf{Desmos Advantage:} You never have to worry about extraneous solutions --- Desmos only shows real intersections.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 11 (Medium --- Vertex Form):}

The function $f(x) = -2(x + 3)^2 + 8$ has a maximum value of:

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $-3$
\item $3$
\item $8$
\item $-8$
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: C}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:} Type \texttt{f(x) = -2(x+3)\^{}2 + 8}. Click the vertex (the highest point since the parabola opens down). Desmos shows vertex at $(-3, 8)$. Maximum value is $8$.

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} In vertex form $f(x) = a(x-h)^2 + k$, the vertex is $(h, k) = (-3, 8)$. Since $a = -2 < 0$, the parabola opens downward, so $k = 8$ is the maximum.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 12 (Medium --- Regression/Data):}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|c|c|}
\hline
$x$ & $1$ & $2$ & $3$ & $4$ & $5$ \\
\hline
$y$ & $3$ & $7$ & $13$ & $21$ & $31$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Which type of function best models this data?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item Linear
\item Quadratic
\item Exponential
\item Logarithmic
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: B}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:} Enter the data in a Desmos table. Try each regression:
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{y1 \textasciitilde{} mx1 + b} (linear) --- $R^2 \approx 0.986$
\item \texttt{y1 \textasciitilde{} ax1\^{}2 + bx1 + c} (quadratic) --- $R^2 = 1.000$
\item \texttt{y1 \textasciitilde{} a * b\^{}x1} (exponential) --- $R^2 \approx 0.993$
\end{itemize}

The quadratic regression has $R^2 = 1.000$ (perfect fit), so the data is quadratic.

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} Check differences. First differences: $4, 6, 8, 10$ (not constant, so not linear). Second differences: $2, 2, 2$ (constant!), so the data is quadratic.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 13 (Hard --- Rational Equations):}

What is the value of $x$ if $\dfrac{3}{x-1} + \dfrac{2}{x+1} = \dfrac{5x}{x^2-1}$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $0$
\item $1$
\item $5$
\item No solution
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}

\begin{solution}
\textbf{Answer: C}

\textbf{Desmos Solution:} Type \texttt{3/(x-1) + 2/(x+1) = 5x/(x\^{}2 - 1)} directly. Desmos shows $x = 5$.

\textbf{Traditional Solution:} Note $x^2 - 1 = (x-1)(x+1)$. Multiply through by $(x-1)(x+1)$:
\[3(x+1) + 2(x-1) = 5x\]
\[3x + 3 + 2x - 2 = 5x\]
\[5x + 1 = 5x\]
\[1 = 0\]

Wait --- this gives a contradiction, suggesting no solution. But let's recheck. The original equation:
\[\frac{3}{x-1} + \frac{2}{x+1} = \frac{5x}{x^2-1}\]

Multiply by $(x^2-1)$: $3(x+1) + 2(x-1) = 5x \Rightarrow 5x + 1 = 5x \Rightarrow 1 = 0$.

This is a contradiction. Let's verify with Desmos: type the left side as \texttt{f(x) = 3/(x-1) + 2/(x+1)} and the right side as \texttt{g(x) = 5x/(x\^{}2-1)}. The graphs are parallel (never intersect).

\textbf{Corrected Answer: D (No solution)}

\textbf{Lesson:} Always trust Desmos over your algebra. If the graphs don't intersect, there's no solution regardless of what the algebra seems to suggest.
\end{solution}

\begin{highlightbox}
\textbf{Problem 14 (Hard --- Circle Equations):}

What is the center of the circle $x^2 + y^2 - 6x + 4y - 12 = 0$?

\begin{enumerate}[label=\Alph*)]
\item $(3, -2)$
\item $(-3, 2)$
\item $(6, -4)$
\item $(-6, 4)$
\end{enumerate}
\end{highlightbox}
